     <p>The <b>University of British Columbia</b> (commonly referred to as <b>UBC</b>) is a Canadian <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> with campuses and facilities in <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>. It is the oldest institution of higher learning in the province of British Columbia and has the largest enrollment with over 57,000 students at its <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Okanagan" title="Okanagan">Okanagan</a> campuses combined.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was incorporated in Vancouver in 1908 as the McGill University College of British Columbia, and granted <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">McGill University</a> degrees until it became the independent <b>University of British Columbia</b> in 1915. <sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> UBC's main 4.02&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (993-acre) <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> campus is located within the <a href="/wiki/University_Endowment_Lands" title="University Endowment Lands">University Endowment Lands</a>, about 10&nbsp;km (6.2&nbsp;mi) from <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Vancouver" title="Downtown Vancouver">Downtown Vancouver</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-facts1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts1-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2.09&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (516-acre) <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Okanagan" title="University of British Columbia Okanagan">Kelowna campus</a>, open since 2005, is located in the <a href="/wiki/Okanagan" title="Okanagan">Okanagan Valley</a>.</p> 
     <p>As of the 2012-2013 school year, UBC was ranked 2nd in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> among all its major/research universities offering medical and doctoral degrees in the <i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> 22nd annual rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was also ranked 30th worldwide (and 2nd in Canada) in the 2012?2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i>, 39th worldwide (and 2nd in Canada) in the 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i>, and 8th overall (and 2nd among Canadian universities) in <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i>'s ranking of top universities outside of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-timeshighereducation.co.uk_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeshighereducation.co.uk-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-newsb_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsb-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, UBC reported the highest entrance requirements for undergraduate admission in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> UBC faculty, alumni, and researchers have won seven <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">Nobel Prizes</a>, 67 <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarships" title="Rhodes Scholarships" class="mw-redirect">Rhodes Scholarships</a>, 64 <a href="/wiki/Olympic_medals" title="Olympic medals" class="mw-redirect">Olympic medals</a>, and alumni include two <a href="/wiki/Canadian_prime_ministers" title="Canadian prime ministers" class="mw-redirect">Canadian prime ministers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-facts1_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts1-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>All of UBC's faculties, alone or jointly, exhibit very high research activity. The university is consistently included among the top three research universities in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> and among the top research universities in the world, both in terms of quality and quantity of research.<sup id="cite_ref-publicaffairs.ubc.ca_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-publicaffairs.ubc.ca-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_year" title="Fiscal year">fiscal year</a> 2012, UBC reported $519 million per year in research funding, involving over 16,000 faculty and staff.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> A founding member of the <a href="/wiki/U15_(universities)" title="U15 (universities)" class="mw-redirect">U15</a>, UBC attracts research funding from government, non-profit organizations and industry through approximately 8,000 projects.<sup id="cite_ref-publicaffairs.ubc.ca_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-publicaffairs.ubc.ca-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The university encompasses twenty-six faculties and schools at its Vancouver campus, eight faculties and schools at its Okanagan campus and is affiliated with several research institutes, centres, organizations and hospitals. <sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UBC is a <a href="/wiki/Non-sectarian" title="Non-sectarian" class="mw-redirect">non-sectarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coeducational" title="Coeducational" class="mw-redirect">coeducational</a> institution, with more than 275,000 living alumni in 120 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is a member of <a href="/wiki/Universitas_21" title="Universitas 21">Universitas 21</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Universities_and_Colleges_of_Canada" title="Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada">Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Institutions_of_Higher_Learning" title="Association of Southeast Asian Institutions of Higher Learning">Association of Southeast Asian Institutions of Higher Learning</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Universities" title="International Association of Universities">International Association of Universities</a>, the <a href="/wiki/U15_(universities)" title="U15 (universities)" class="mw-redirect">U15</a> and the only Canadian member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Pacific_Rim_Universities" title="Association of Pacific Rim Universities">Association of Pacific Rim Universities</a>. The university's varsity teams, known as the <a href="/wiki/UBC_Thunderbirds" title="UBC Thunderbirds">Thunderbirds</a>, compete in the <a href="/wiki/Canada_West_Universities_Athletic_Association" title="Canada West Universities Athletic Association">Canada West Universities Athletic Association</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">Canadian Interuniversity Sport</a>.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_and_early_years">Foundation and early years</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Foundation and early years">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <table class="rquote floatright" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:right; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;"> 
        <td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em;">?</td> 
        <td style="padding:0 10px;">The University shall... provide for: Such instruction in all branches of liberal education as may enable students to become proficient in... science, commerce, arts, literature, law, medicine, and all other branches of knowledge</td> 
        <td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em;">?</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px;"> <p style="font-size:smaller; line-height:1em; text-align:right">?<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>, An Act to Establish and Incorporate a University for the Province of British Columbia, <i>Acts of 1908, Chapter 53</i></p> </td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UBC_Fairview_campus_(c._1917).gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif/220px-UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif/330px-UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif/440px-UBC_Fairview_campus_%28c._1917%29.gif 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UBC_Fairview_campus_(c._1917).gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> View of the UBC Fairview campus from the roof of King Edward High School (photo by Canadian Photo Co.)
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg/220px-Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg/330px-Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg/440px-Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Sharp_and_Thompson_proposed_plan_for_the_UBC_Point_Grey_campus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Original 1914 plan of the UBC campus, by architects Sharp and Thompson
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1877, only six years after British Columbia joined Canada, Superintendent of Education John Jessop submitted a proposal for the formation of a provincial university. <i>An Act Respecting the University of British Columbia</i> was passed by the provincial legislature in 1890, but disagreements arose over whether to build the university on <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Island" title="Vancouver Island">Vancouver Island</a> or the mainland. A provincial university was formally called into being by the <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia_University_Act" title="British Columbia University Act" class="mw-redirect">British Columbia University Act</a> of 1908, although its location was not yet specified.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The governance was modelled on the provincial University of Toronto Act of 1906 which established a bicameral system of university government consisting of a senate (faculty), responsible for academic policy, and a board of governors (citizens) exercising exclusive control over financial policy and having formal authority in all other matters. The president, appointed by the board, was to provide a link between the two bodies and to perform institutional leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The Act constituted a twenty-one member senate with Francis Carter-Cotton of Vancouver as Chancellor.</p> 
     <p>Before the University Act, there had been several attempts at establishing a degree-granting university with assistance from the Universities of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">Toronto</a> and <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">McGill</a>. Columbian College in New Westminster, through its affiliation with <a href="/wiki/Victoria_University_in_the_University_of_Toronto" title="Victoria University in the University of Toronto" class="mw-redirect">Victoria College of the University of Toronto</a>, began to offer university-level credit at the turn-of-the-century, but it was McGill that would come to dominate higher education in the early 1900s.</p> 
     <p>Building on a successful affiliation between Vancouver and Victoria high schools with <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">McGill University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Marshall_Tory" title="Henry Marshall Tory">Henry Marshall Tory</a><sup id="cite_ref-Tory_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tory-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> helped to establish the McGill University College of British Columbia. From 1906 to 1915 McGill BC (as it was called) operated as a private institution providing the first few years toward a degree at McGill University or elsewhere. The Henry Marshall Tory Medal was established in 1941 by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Marshall_Tory" title="Henry Marshall Tory">Henry Marshall Tory</a> (1864?1947), FRSC, founding President of the University of Alberta and of the National Research Council of Canada, and a co-founder of Carleton University.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg/220px-Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg" width="220" height="291" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg/330px-Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Carleton_pres_Tory.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Henry_Marshall_Tory" title="Henry Marshall Tory">Henry Marshall Tory</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In the meantime, appeals were again made to the government to revive the earlier legislation for a provincial institution, leading to the University Endowment Act in 1907, and The University Act in 1908. In 1910 the Point Grey site was chosen, and the government appointed Dr. <a href="/wiki/Frank_Wesbrook" title="Frank Wesbrook">Frank Fairchild Wesbrook</a> as President in 1913. A declining economy and the outbreak of war in August 1914 compelled the University to postpone plans for building at Point Grey, and instead the former McGill University College site at <a href="/wiki/Fairview_(Vancouver)" title="Fairview (Vancouver)" class="mw-redirect">Fairview</a> became home to the University until 1925. The first day of lectures was September 30, 1915, the new independent university absorbing McGill University College. University of British Columbia awarded its first degrees in 1916.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Move_to_Point_Grey">Move to Point Grey</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Move to Point Grey">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>World War I dominated campus life, and the student body was &quot;decimated&quot; by enlistments for active service, with three hundred UBC students in Company &quot;D&quot; alone. By the end of the war, 697 members of the University had enlisted. A total of 109 students graduated in the three war-time congregations, all but one in the Faculty of Arts and Science.</p> 
     <p>By 1920, the university had only three faculties: Arts, Applied Science, and Agriculture (with Departments of <a href="/wiki/Agronomy" title="Agronomy">Agronomy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Animal_Husbandry" title="Animal Husbandry" class="mw-redirect">Animal Husbandry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dairying" title="Dairying" class="mw-redirect">Dairying</a>, Horticulture and Poultry). It only awarded the degrees of Bachelor of Arts (B.A.), <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Applied_Science" title="Bachelor of Applied Science">Bachelor of Applied Science</a> (B.A.Sc.), and Bachelor of Science in Agriculture (B.S.A.).<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> There were 576 male students and 386 female students in the 1920?21 winter session, but only 64 academic staff, including 6 women.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the early part of the twentieth century, professional education expanded beyond the traditional fields of theology, law and medicine. UBC provided no degrees in these areas, but was beginning to offer degrees in new professional areas such as engineering, agriculture, nursing, and school teaching. Graduate training based on the German-inspired American model of specialized course work and the completion of a research thesis was introduced, with students completing M.A. degrees in natural sciences, social sciences, and humanities.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif/220px-UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif/330px-UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif/440px-UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UBC_Great_Trek_at_Granville_and_Georgia_streets.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Students march down Granville street during the Great Trek
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 1922, the now twelve-hundred-strong student body embarked on a &quot;Build the University&quot; campaign. Students marched in the streets of Vancouver to draw attention to their plight, enlist popular support, and embarrass the government. Fifty-six thousand signatures were presented at legislature in support of the campaign, which was ultimately successful. On September 22, 1925, lectures began on the new Point Grey campus. Except for the Library, Science and Power House buildings, all the campus buildings were temporary constructions. Two playing fields were built by the students themselves, but the University had no dormitories and no social centre. Still, the University continued to grow steadily.</p> 
     <p>Soon, however, the effects of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression_in_Canada" title="Great Depression in Canada">depression</a> began to be felt. The provincial government, upon which the University depended heavily, cut the annual grant severely. In 1932?33 salaries were cut by up to 23%. Posts remained vacant, and a few faculty lost their jobs. Most graduate courses were dropped. In 1935, the University established the Department of Extension. Just as things began to improve, World War II broke out. Canada declared war on September 10, 1939. Soon afterwards, University President Klinck wrote:</p> 
     <blockquote> 
      <p><i>From the day of the declaration of war, the University has been prepared to put at the disposal of the Government all possible assistance by way of laboratories, equipment and trained personnel, insofar as such action is consistent with the maintenance of reasonably efficient instructional standards. To do less would be unthinkable.</i></p> 
     </blockquote> 
     <p>Heavy rains and melting snowfall eroded a deep ravine across the north end of the campus, in the Grand Campus Washout of 1935. The campus did not yet have <a href="/wiki/Storm_drain" title="Storm drain">storm drains</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Surface_runoff" title="Surface runoff">surface runoff</a> went down a ravine to the beach. When the University carved a ditch to drain flooding on University Avenue, the rush of water steepened the ravine and eroded it back as fast as 10 feet (3.0&nbsp;m) per hour. The resulting gully eventually consumed 100,000 cubic yards (76,455&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>), two bridges, and buildings near <a href="/wiki/Green_College,_University_of_British_Columbia" title="Green College, University of British Columbia">Graham House</a>. The University was closed for 4&frac12; days. Afterwards, the gully was filled with debris from a nearby landslide, and only traces are visible today.<sup id="cite_ref-Williams_1966_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams_1966-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Recruit_training" title="Recruit training">Military training</a> on the campus became popular, then mandatory. WWII marked the first provision of money from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Canada" title="Government of Canada">federal government</a> to the University for research purposes.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Postwar_Years">Postwar Years</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Postwar Years">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>By the end of the war, it became clear that the facilities at Point Grey had become totally inadequate to cater to the huge influx of veterans returning to their studies. The University needed new staff, new courses, new faculties, and new buildings for teaching and accommodation. The student population rose from 2,974 in 1944?45 to 9,374 in 1947?48. Surplus <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Army" title="Canadian Army">Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Force" title="Royal Canadian Air Force">Air Force</a> camps were used for both classrooms and accommodation. Fifteen complete camps were taken over by the University in the course of the 1945?46 session alone, with a sixteenth camp situated on <a href="/wiki/Little_Mountain_(Vancouver)" title="Little Mountain (Vancouver)" class="mw-redirect">Little Mountain</a> in Vancouver, converted into suites for married students. Most of the camps were dismantled and carried by barge or truck to the University where the huts were scattered across the campus. (A few huts remain in place today!)</p> 
     <p>Student numbers hit 9,374 in 1948; more than 53% of the students were <a href="/wiki/Veteran" title="Veteran">war veterans</a> in 1947?67. Between 1947 and 1951 twenty new permanent buildings were erected.</p> 
     <p>The War Memorial Hall (more generally known as Memorial Hall) and War Memorial Gym are landmark buildings on the campus of the University of British Columbia. The lecture hall, theatre and gym were the result of a student alumni campaign to honour men and women of British Columbia who served in the First World War and Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The War Memorial gymnasium was officially dedicated on October 26, 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg/220px-Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg/330px-Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg/440px-Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Raven-and-the-first-men.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Bill_Reid" title="Bill Reid">Bill Reid</a>'s Raven and The First Men at the 
        <a href="/wiki/UBC_Museum_of_Anthropology" title="UBC Museum of Anthropology" class="mw-redirect">UBC Museum of Anthropology</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The single-university policy in the West was changed as existing colleges of the provincial universities gained autonomy as universities ? the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Victoria" title="University of Victoria">University of Victoria</a> was established in 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>On February 10, 1964 Harvey Reginald MacMillan donated $8.2 million for postgraduate education to the university.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Anthropology_at_UBC" title="Museum of Anthropology at UBC">Museum of Anthropology</a> at UBC was announced on July 1, 1971 by Prime Minister Trudeau. At a construction cost of $2.5 million, the museum building designed by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Erickson" title="Arthur Erickson">Arthur Erickson</a> opened in 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UBC's current president is <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Toope" title="Stephen Toope">Dr. Stephen Toope</a>, appointed on July 1, 2006. He succeeded <a href="/wiki/Martha_Piper" title="Martha Piper">Dr. Martha Piper</a>, who was the University's first female president and the first non-Canadian born president. The Chancellor of the University, who acts as the University's ceremonial head and sits on the academic Senate and the Board of Governors, is Sarah Morgan-Silvester (as of July 1, 2008).<sup id="cite_ref-UBC_2008-04-14_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UBC_2008-04-14-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Okanagan_Campus" title="University of British Columbia Okanagan Campus" class="mw-redirect">UBC Okanagan</a> campus is led by Dr. Doug Owram, Deputy Vice-Chancellor. All three founding faculties remain, but the Faculty of Agriculture is now known as the Faculty of Land &amp; Food Systems.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UBC_aerial_view.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/UBC_aerial_view.jpg/220px-UBC_aerial_view.jpg" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/UBC_aerial_view.jpg/330px-UBC_aerial_view.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/UBC_aerial_view.jpg/440px-UBC_aerial_view.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">

      </div>

         <a href="/wiki/File:Irving_K._Barber_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Irving K. Barber Library and Ladner Clock Tower
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vancouver">Vancouver</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Vancouver">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Vancouver campus is located at <a href="/wiki/Point_Grey" title="Point Grey" class="mw-redirect">Point Grey</a>, a twenty-minute drive from downtown Vancouver. It is near several beaches and has views of the <a href="/wiki/North_Shore_Mountains" title="North Shore Mountains">North Shore mountains</a>. The 7.63&nbsp;km&sup2; <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Spirit_Regional_Park" title="Pacific Spirit Regional Park">Pacific Spirit Regional Park</a> serves as a green-belt between the campus and the city. Buildings on the Vancouver campus currently occupy 1,091,997 m&sup2; gross, located on 1.7&nbsp;km&sup2; of maintained land. The campus street plan is mostly in a grid of malls (for driving and pedestrian-only). Lower Mall and West Mall are in the southwestern part of the peninsula, with Main, East, and Wesbrook Malls northeast of them.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_Endowment_Lands" title="University Endowment Lands">University Endowment Lands</a> are not within Vancouver's city limits, and therefore UBC is policed by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Mounted_Police" title="Royal Canadian Mounted Police">RCMP</a> rather than the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Police_Department" title="Vancouver Police Department">Vancouver Police Department</a>. However, the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Fire_and_Rescue_Services" title="Vancouver Fire and Rescue Services">Vancouver Fire Department</a> provides service to UBC under a contract. In addition to UBC RCMP, UBC have Campus Security, that patrol the campus. Postage sent to any building on campus includes Vancouver in the address. UBC Vancouver also has two satellite campuses within the City of Vancouver: a campus at <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_General_Hospital" title="Vancouver General Hospital">Vancouver General Hospital</a> for the medical sciences, and UBC <a href="/wiki/Robson_Square" title="Robson Square">Robson Square</a> in downtown Vancouver for part-time credit and non-credit programmes. UBC is also a partner in the consortium backing <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Way_Campus_Ltd" title="Great Northern Way Campus Ltd" class="mw-redirect">Great Northern Way Campus Ltd</a>, and is affiliated with a group of adjacent theological colleges, which include the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_School_of_Theology" title="Vancouver School of Theology">Vancouver School of Theology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regent_College" title="Regent College">Regent College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carey_Theological_College" title="Carey Theological College">Carey Theological College</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Corpus_Christi_College_(Vancouver)" title="Corpus Christi College (Vancouver)">Corpus Christi College</a>.</p> 
     <p>The campus is home to numerous gardens. The <a href="/wiki/UBC_Botanical_Garden_and_Centre_for_Plant_Research" title="UBC Botanical Garden and Centre for Plant Research">UBC Botanical Garden and Centre for Plant Research</a>, the first UBC department, holds a collection of over 8000 different kinds of plants used for research, conservation and education. The original site of the UBC botanical garden was at the &quot;Old Arboretum&quot;. Today all that remains of it are trees planted in 1916 by <a href="/wiki/John_Davidson_(botanist)" title="John Davidson (botanist)">John Davidson</a>. The old arboretum is now home to many buildings including the First Nations House of Learning. The <a href="/wiki/Nitobe_Memorial_Garden" title="Nitobe Memorial Garden">Nitobe Memorial Garden</a>, built to honour Japanese scholar <a href="/wiki/Inazo_Nitobe" title="Inazo Nitobe" class="mw-redirect">Inazo Nitobe</a>, the garden has been the subject of more than fifteen years' study by a UBC professor,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words" class="mw-redirect"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2012)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> who believes that its construction hides a number of impressive features, including references to Japanese philosophy and mythology, shadow bridges visible only at certain times of year, and positioning of a lantern that is filled with light at the exact date and time of Nitobe's death each year. The garden is behind the university's Asian Centre, which is built using steel girders from Japan's exhibit at <a href="/wiki/Expo_%2770" title="Expo '70">Osaka Expo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Library_History_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library_History-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Vancouver_school_of_theology_(UBC-2009).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG/220px-Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG/330px-Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG/440px-Vancouver_school_of_theology_%28UBC-2009%29.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Vancouver_school_of_theology_(UBC-2009).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The UBC Vancouver School of Theology, built in 1927
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The campus also features the <a href="/wiki/Chan_Centre_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Chan Centre for the Performing Arts">Chan Centre for the Performing Arts</a>: a <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">performing arts</a> centre containing the <a href="/wiki/Chan_Shun_Concert_Hall" title="Chan Shun Concert Hall" class="mw-redirect">Chan Shun Concert Hall</a>, Telus Studio Theatre and the Royal Bank Cinema. It is often the location of convocation ceremonies as well as the filming location for the <a href="/wiki/4400_Center" title="4400 Center" class="mw-redirect">4400 Center</a> on the television show <i><a href="/wiki/The_4400" title="The 4400">The 4400</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as the Madacorp entrance set on <i><a href="/wiki/Kyle_XY" title="Kyle XY">Kyle XY</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> It has also been featured as the Cloud 9 Ballroom in the re-imagined <i><a href="/wiki/Battlestar_Galactica" title="Battlestar Galactica">Battlestar Galactica</a></i> (Season 1, Episode 11: <i>Colonial Day</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Okanagan">Okanagan</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Okanagan">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Engineering_Management_and_Education_(UBC_Okanagan).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg/220px-Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg/330px-Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg/440px-Engineering_Management_and_Education_%28UBC_Okanagan%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Engineering_Management_and_Education_(UBC_Okanagan).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Engineering, Management and Education (EME) Complex at 
        <a href="/wiki/UBC_Okanagan" title="UBC Okanagan" class="mw-redirect">UBC Okanagan</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Okanagan" title="University of British Columbia Okanagan">University of British Columbia Okanagan</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Okanagan" title="University of British Columbia Okanagan">Okanagan Campus</a>, is located on the former North Kelowna Campus of <a href="/wiki/Okanagan_University_College" title="Okanagan University College">Okanagan University College</a>, next to <a href="/wiki/Kelowna_International_Airport" title="Kelowna International Airport">Kelowna International Airport</a> on the north-east side of <a href="/wiki/Kelowna" title="Kelowna">Kelowna</a>, British Columbia.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> This campus offers undergraduate degrees in Arts, Science, Nursing, Education, Management and Engineering as well as graduate degrees in most of these subject. The Okanagan campus is experiencing a $450 million CDN expansion with construction of several new residential, teaching and research buildings.</p> 
     <p>In 2010, UBC Okanagan campus doubled in size from 105 ha. to 208.6 ha.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries.2C_archives_and_galleries">Libraries, archives and galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Libraries, archives and galleries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Library" title="University of British Columbia Library">University of British Columbia Library</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The UBC Library, which comprises 5.8 million books and journals, 5.3 million microforms, over 833,000 maps, videos and other multimedia materials and over 46,700 subscriptions, is the second largest research library in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-about_the_library_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about_the_library-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The libraries lent out over 2.5 million print works in 2008/2009 with over 2.9 million visits to the library (measured by gate counters).<sup id="cite_ref-librarian_report_2009_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-librarian_report_2009-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The library has twenty-one branches and divisions at UBC and at other locations, including three branches at teaching hospitals (<a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_Hospital_(Vancouver)" title="St. Paul's Hospital (Vancouver)">St. Paul's Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Hospital_and_Health_Sciences_Centre" title="Vancouver Hospital and Health Sciences Centre">Vancouver Hospital and Health Sciences Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/BC_Children%27s_Hospital" title="BC Children's Hospital" class="mw-redirect">BC Children's Hospital</a>), one at UBC's <a href="/wiki/Robson_Square" title="Robson Square">Robson Square</a> campus in downtown Vancouver, and one at the UBC's <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Okanagan" title="University of British Columbia Okanagan">Okanagan Campus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-about_the_library_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-about_the_library-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Plans are also under way to establish a library at the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_Way_Campus" title="Great Northern Way Campus">Great Northern Way Campus</a> on the Finning Lands.</p> 
     <p>The former Main Library has undergone construction and has been renamed the <a href="/wiki/Irving_K._Barber_Learning_Centre" title="Irving K. Barber Learning Centre">Irving K. Barber Learning Centre</a>. The new library incorporates the centre heritage block of the old Main Library with two new expansion wings and features an <a href="/wiki/Automated_storage_and_retrieval_system" title="Automated storage and retrieval system">automated storage and retrieval system</a> (ASRS), the first of its kind in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Major General <a href="/wiki/Victor_Odlum" title="Victor Odlum">Victor Odlum</a> CB, CMG, DSO, VD donated his personal library of 10,000 books, which has been housed in &quot;the Rockwoods Centre Library&quot; of the UBC library since 1963.</p> 
     <p>The AHVA Library Gallery presents Contemporary, Fine Art exhibitions and Artists talks and showcases the work of student and faculty artists in Studio Art, Art History and Curatorial Studies programs of the UBC Department of Art History, Visual Art and Theory.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Morris and Helen Belkin Art Gallery at the UBC houses the university's collection of three archives and fine art; 1,000 works, mainly Canadian contemporary pieces 1960 to the present. The Gallery houses exhibitions, publications, acquisitions, archival projects, lectures and symposia on art history, criticism, and curating.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance_and_academics">Governance and academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Governance and academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UBC_-_Walter_C._Koerner_Library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/UBC_-_Walter_C._Koerner_Library.jpg/220px-UBC_-_Walter_C._Koerner_Library.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/UBC_-_Walter_C._Koerner_Library.jpg/330px-UBC_-_Walter_C._Koerner_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/UBC_-_Walter_C._Koerner_Library.jpg/440px-UBC_-_Walter_C._Koerner_Library.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UBC_-_Walter_C._Koerner_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Walter C. Koerner Library, designed by UBC alumnus 
        <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Erickson" title="Arthur Erickson">Arthur Erickson</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The administration of UBC, as mandated by the University Act, is composed of a chancellor, convocation, board, senate, and faculties of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-University_Act_2009-08-05_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-University_Act_2009-08-05-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The Board of Governors is responsible for the management of property and revenue, while the Senate is vested with managing the academic operation of the university. Both are composed of faculty and students who are elected to the position. Degrees and diplomas are conferred by the convocation, which is composed of alumni, administrators, and faculty, with a quorum of twenty members. UBC also has a President, who is a chief executive officer of the university and a member of the Senate, Board of Governors, Convocation, and also serves as Vice Chancellor. The President of the University is responsible for managing the academic operation of the university, including recommending appointments, calling meetings of faculties, and establishing committees.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculties_and_schools">Faculties and schools</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Faculties and schools">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UBC%27s_Chembuilding.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/UBC%27s_Chembuilding.jpg/220px-UBC%27s_Chembuilding.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/UBC%27s_Chembuilding.jpg/330px-UBC%27s_Chembuilding.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/UBC%27s_Chembuilding.jpg/440px-UBC%27s_Chembuilding.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UBC%27s_Chembuilding.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The chemistry building, built in 1925
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Faculties_and_Schools_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia" title="Faculties and Schools of the University of British Columbia">Faculties and Schools of the University of British Columbia</a>
     </div> 
     <p>UBC's academic activity is organized into &quot;faculties&quot; and &quot;schools&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Currently, UBC has twelve faculties at its Vancouver campus and seven faculties at its Okanagan campus.<sup id="cite_ref-facts1_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts1-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> UBC Vancouver has two academic colleges: Interdisciplinary Studies and Health Disciplines, while UBC Okanagan has a College of Graduate Studies. At the Vancouver campus, the Faculty of Arts, which dates back to the 1915 Fairview Campus, is the largest faculty with twenty departments and schools. With the split of the Faculty of Arts and Science in 1964, the Faculty of Science is the second largest faculty with nine departments. The <a href="/wiki/Sauder_School_of_Business" title="Sauder School of Business">Sauder School of Business</a> is UBC's Faculty of Commerce and Business Administration. The School of Architecture offers a program in architecture accredited by the Canadian Architectural Certification Board at both the bachelor level (B.Arch.) and the master's level (M.Arch.).<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> As of December 2012, a new school was created: <a href="/wiki/UBC_Vancouver_School_of_Economics" title="UBC Vancouver School of Economics">UBC Vancouver School of Economics</a> in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/Sauder_School_of_Business" title="Sauder School of Business">Sauder School of Business</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Enrollment">Enrollment</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Enrollment">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg/220px-Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg" width="220" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg/330px-Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg/440px-Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Chan_centre_performing_arts_concert_tessler.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Chan Centre for Performing Arts, designed by 
        <a href="/wiki/Bing_Thom" title="Bing Thom">Bing Thom</a>, B.Arch '66
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 2011, UBC had 3,331 full-time <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(division)" title="Faculty (division)">Faculty</a>, and 10,652 non-faculty employees. It had over fifty six thousand students (48,726 <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_student" title="Undergraduate student" class="mw-redirect">undergraduate students</a> and 10,686 <a href="/wiki/Graduate_student" title="Graduate student" class="mw-redirect">graduate students</a>), and more than 275,000 alumni in 120 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-facts1_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts1-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The requirements for admission differ between students from British Columbia, other provinces in Canada, and international students due to the lack of uniformity in marking schemes. In 2003 the <a href="/wiki/National_Post" title="National Post">National Post</a> stated that the university had the highest entrance requirements for undergraduate admission out of all universities in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-Post_2003_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Post_2003-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The secondary school average for full-time first-year students at the university in 2009?2010 was 89.5 percent for the Vancouver campus, and 82.2% for the Okanagan campus.<sup id="cite_ref-facts1_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts1-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The acceptance rate at the university for domestic full-time, first-year applications in 2011 was 50.6 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
