     <p>UBC is consistently ranked as one of the world's leading universities.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thedailybeast.com_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thedailybeast.com-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2012?2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i> ranked the university 30th overall, 22nd in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a><sup id="cite_ref-timeshighereducation.co.uk_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeshighereducation.co.uk-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> ranked the university 39th overall, 31st in North America and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_CAN-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a>'</i>s 2011 global university rankings, the university was ranked 8th among institutions outside the United States, and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-thedailybeast.com_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thedailybeast.com-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was also ranked 45th in the world and third in Canada in the 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i> and the 2012-2013 <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i> 's Top 400 Universities.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, the 2013 Webometrics Ranking of World Universities ranked UBC 1st in Canada and 22nd in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of national rankings, <i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> ranked the university second in their 2013 Medical Doctoral university rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-Macdoc_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macdoc-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> UBC was also ranked in spite of having opted out?along with several other universities in Canada?of participating in <i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> graduate survey since 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> As of the 2012?2013 school year, the <a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_Canada#Higher_Education_Strategy_Associates.27_rankings" title="Rankings of universities in Canada">Higher Education Strategy Associates</a> ranked UBC first Science and Engineering, and first in Social Sciences and Humanities.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A number of individual academic fields at the university have also received high rankings both nationally and internationally. The 2012?2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i> lists the university 19th in the world and first in Canada in the field of <a href="/wiki/Social_sciences" title="Social sciences" class="mw-redirect">social sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> In particular, the <a href="/wiki/UBC_Vancouver_School_of_Economics" title="UBC Vancouver School of Economics">UBC Vancouver School of Economics</a> is ranked the best in Canada and among the top 30 <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">Economics</a> departments in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> UBC's Department of <a href="/wiki/Political_Science" title="Political Science" class="mw-redirect">Political Science</a> is also well reputed, both nationally and among world universities. In 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i> ranked UBC 22nd worldwide in the field of Politics and International Relations.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2011 ARWU rankings for social sciences, the university was ranked 32nd in the world and first in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SOC_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SOC-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> In the field of life sciences, the 2012?2013 Times rankings placed the university 20th in the world, and first nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-UnivRankings_THES_Life_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnivRankings_THES_Life-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2011 ARWU rankings for life sciences placed the university 36th in the world and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_LIFE_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_LIFE-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> In natural sciences and mathematics, the university was ranked 51?75th in the world, and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SCI_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_SCI-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> In the field of physical sciences, the Times rankings placed the university 35th in the world, and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-UnivRankings_THES_NatSci_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnivRankings_THES_NatSci-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, in the field of engineering and technology, UBC placed 33rd in the world and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-UnivRankings_THES_Tech_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnivRankings_THES_Tech-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Finally, the 2012?2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i> ranked the university 40th in the world and third in Canada in the field of arts and humanities.<sup id="cite_ref-UnivRankings_THES_Arts_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnivRankings_THES_Arts-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Faculty_of_Law" title="University of British Columbia Faculty of Law">law faculty</a> was ranked fifth in <i>Maclean's</i> 2012 rankings of Canadian <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a> schools, and 22nd in the world and 3rd in Canada in the 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i> by Subject: Law.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sauder_School_of_Business" title="Sauder School of Business">Sauder School of Business</a> has also received accolades both nationally and internationally. The business school appeared on the 2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i> global MBA rankings, placing 57nd in the world, and third in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The business school was also ranked in QS's 2012 North American MBA rankings, placing 18th in North America, and third in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of British Columbia is a member of <a href="/wiki/Universitas_21" title="Universitas 21">Universitas 21</a>, an international association of research-led institutions, as well as the only Canadian member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Pacific_Rim_Universities" title="Association of Pacific Rim Universities">Association of Pacific Rim Universities</a>, a consortium of 42 leading research universities in the Pacific Rim.<sup id="cite_ref-universitas_21_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-universitas_21-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-apru_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apru-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> With a sponsored research income of $538.398 million, the university manages the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Funding_of_science" title="Funding of science">research budget</a> of any university in Canada. With an average research income of $234,000 CAD per full-time faculty member, the university is also the second most research intensive full-service university in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of research performance, <a href="/wiki/High_Impact_Universities" title="High Impact Universities">High Impact Universities</a> 2010 ranked the university 30th out of 500 universities, and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Higher_Education_Evaluation_and_Accreditation_Council_of_Taiwan" title="Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan">Higher Education Evaluation and Accreditation Council of Taiwan</a> (HEEACT), an organization which also evaluates universities based on their scientific paper's performances, ranked the university 29th in the world and second in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university operates and manages a number of research centres. In 1972, a consortium made up of the University of British Columbia, and four other universities from Alberta and British Columbia established the <a href="/wiki/Bamfield_Marine_Sciences_Centre" title="Bamfield Marine Sciences Centre">Bamfield Marine Sciences Centre</a>. Located on Vancouver Island, the centre provides year-round research facilities and technical assistance for biologists, ecologists and oceanographers.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Peter_Wall_Institute_for_Advanced_Studies" title="Peter Wall Institute for Advanced Studies">Peter Wall Institute for Advanced Studies</a> is an interdisciplinary research institute for fundamental research in the Sciences, Social Sciences, and Humanities. The <a href="/wiki/UBC_Farm" title="UBC Farm">UBC Farm</a> is a 24 hectare learning and research farm located in UBC's South Campus area is the only working farmland within the city of Vancouver. The farm features Saturday Farm Markets from early June until early October, selling organic produce and eggs to the community. <a href="/wiki/TRIUMF" title="TRIUMF">TRIUMF</a>, a laboratory specializing in <a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">particle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear physics</a> is also located at the university. The name was formerly an acronym for TRI-University Meson Facility, but TRIUMF is now owned and operated by a consortium of eleven Canadian universities. The consortium runs TRIUMF through a contribution of funds from the <a href="/wiki/National_Research_Council_of_Canada" title="National Research Council of Canada" class="mw-redirect">National Research Council of Canada</a>, and makes TRIUMF?s facilities available to Canadian scientists and to scientists from around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UBC has been ranked in the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_Knights" title="Corporate Knights">Corporate Knights</a> school rankings, which ranks universities based on how they integrate sustainability into the learning experience. The rankings adopt a broad definition of sustainability which encompasses both environmental and social concerns. In the 2011 rankings, UBC was ranked 2nd in the category: top 5 teaching programs.<sup id="cite_ref-CorpK_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CorpK-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> In the ranking of the Canadian law schools, UBC's law school ranked fifth.<sup id="cite_ref-CorpK_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CorpK-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> In the ranking of the MBA programs, Sauder School of Business was ranked fourth in Canada. The same rankings placed the business school 11th in Canada for its undergraduate business program.<sup id="cite_ref-CorpK_88-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CorpK-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University strives to be a world leader in sustainability and sustainable development, aiming to meet the needs of the growing student and faculty population while preserving the environment. The Center for Interactive Research on Sustainability (CIRS) building is a recent addition to the Vancouver campus and it exemplifies the University?s sustainable practices. Developed to create the most sustainable society at UBC, the building has been called the most sustainable, innovative, and high performance building in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-HoldenM_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoldenM-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The CIRS building was first thought of in 2000<sup id="cite_ref-CIRS_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIRS-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> and was the brainchild of Doctor John Robinson, a sustainable development research initiative professor. Robinson worked with faculty members from Emily Carr, Simon Fraser University, and British Columbia Institute of Technology as well as head architect Peter Busby to design the building.<sup id="cite_ref-PlummerR_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PlummerR-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> It cost a total of twenty-three million dollars to complete the 65000 square ? foot building.<sup id="cite_ref-BulaF_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BulaF-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The CIRS building exhibits regenerative sustainability, meaning that the building improves the environment around it.<sup id="cite_ref-RobinsonJ_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RobinsonJ-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> For example, it uses the neighbouring Earth and Ocean Sciences (EOSC) Building in order to heat itself. The EOSC building uses roughly 1600 megawatts of heat energy and goes through ten air changes every hour, wasting around 900 megawatts of that energy.<sup id="cite_ref-CIRS_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIRS-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> The engineers who built the CIRS building saw this as an opportunity; they take the heat that has been expelled from the EOSC building, use 300 megawatts to heat the CIRS building, and send back 600 megawatts to the EOSC building so that it can heat itself. In this way, the CIRS building is restoring its surrounding environment. The CIRS building is designed to be net positive in four ways environmentally, meaning that the processes or products that leave the building are more environmentally friendly than those that go into it.<sup id="cite_ref-HoldenM_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoldenM-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> The best example of the net positivity of the building is the wood it is made of; the wood the building is made of holds within is nearly 600 tons of carbon, this is more carbon than that which has been by the construction of the building, as well as the manufacturing that goes on inside the building today.<sup id="cite_ref-SuzukiD_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SuzukiD-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Other sustainable features of the CIRS building include:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Relies completely on rainwater to supply the whole building</li> 
      <li>An on-site sewage treatment facility that converts all waste created in the building to reusable water and compost</li> 
      <li>The wood used to build the building comes from trees killed by the pine beetle, thus, little logging was needed for construction</li> 
      <li>Relies on mainly solar energy for electricity</li> 
      <li>All areas of the building use natural lighting during the day.<sup id="cite_ref-HoldenM_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HoldenM-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The building integrates ?green,? sustainable and humane features, i.e. not only does it have a small ecological footprint, it also serves as an environment for occupants to be happy, healthy, and productive within.<sup id="cite_ref-PlummerR_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PlummerR-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> This is the direction that the University of British Columbia is moving towards in order to continue their ideas of sustainable development.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aboriginal">Aboriginal</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Aboriginal">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UBC?s Longhouse is the University's centre for <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_peoples_in_Canada" title="Aboriginal peoples in Canada">Aboriginal</a> activities. The university has an Associate Dean of Indigenous Education, and has developed governing board and senate policies as well as Aboriginal governed councils within the university structure.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> UBC offers degrees in First Nations Studies through a program in the Arts Faculty, and a Chinook Diploma Program in the Sauder School of Business; it also runs the Chinook Summer Biz Camp, to foster entrepreneurship among First Nations and M&eacute;tis high school students. It hosts a Bridge Through Sport Program, Summer Science Program, Native Youth Program, and Cedar Day Camp and Afterschool Program. Its First Nations Forestry Initiatives were developed in partnership with specific Aboriginal communities to meet needs in their more remote areas.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>As a public university, UBC is not as dependent on its endowment for operating revenue as some of its international peers. For 2006?2007, UBC had expected a $36 million deficit. With various cost cutting measures, the University posted a small surplus of $1.92 million. As of March 2007, UBC had assets of $3.2 billion and liabilities of $1.8 billion. Total revenue for 2006?2007 was $1.59 billion, of which 36% came from the provincial government, 11% from the federal government, 17% from &quot;sales of goods and services&quot;, 18% from tuition, and 18% from all other sources. Total expenses were $1.50 billion, of which salaries, wages, benefits, and honoraria were 59%, office supplies and expenses were 12%, amortization was 9%, and all other expenses were 20%.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Less than 1% of expenses went to fundraising.<sup id="cite_ref-CRA_tax_return_University_of_British_Columbia_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRA_tax_return_University_of_British_Columbia-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CRA_Charities_Directorate_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRA_Charities_Directorate-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tuition">Tuition</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tuition">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Tuition" title="Tuition" class="mw-redirect">Tuition fees</a> vary significantly between <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canadian</a> citizens (and permanent residents) and international students. In addition, for both undergraduate and graduate programs, tuition rates vary between the university's different faculties. Students must also pay for various living expenses such as housing, food and student healthcare. As of the 2012?2013 school year, these expenses were estimated at around $13,000 CAD per academic year.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate_tuition">Undergraduate tuition</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Undergraduate tuition">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>UBC tuition for 2012 was $4,700 before adding other mandatory administrative fees for a Canadian student in a basic 30-unit program, though various programs cost from $3,406 to $9,640. Tuition for international students is significantly higher (2.3?4.6 times higher than domestic students). In 2012, tuition for international students ranged from $16,245 CAD to $25,721 CAD.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2001?02, UBC had one of the lowest undergraduate <a href="/wiki/Tuition" title="Tuition" class="mw-redirect">tuition</a> rates in Canada, at an average of $2,181 CAD per year for a full-time programme. This was due to a government-instituted tuition freeze. In 2001, however, the BC Liberal party defeated the NDP in British Columbia and lifted the tuition freeze. In 2002?03 undergraduate and graduate tuition rose by an average of 30%, and by up to 40% in some faculties. This has led to better facilities, but also to <a href="/wiki/Student_activism" title="Student activism">student unrest</a> and contributed to a teaching assistant <a href="/wiki/Strike_action" title="Strike action">union strike</a>.</p> 
     <p>UBC again increased tuition by 30% in the 2003?04 year, again by approximately 15% in the 2004?05 season, and 2% in the 2005?06 and 2006?07 years. Increases were lower than expected because, in the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Speech_from_the_Throne" title="Speech from the Throne" class="mw-redirect">Speech from the Throne</a>, the government announced that tuition increases would be capped to inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2006?07, the Canadian average undergraduate tuition fee was $4,347 and the BC average was $4,960.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Graduate_tuition">Graduate tuition</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Graduate tuition">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>In the academic year 2011/2012 most research-based graduate programs assess tuition of $4,263.87 per semester for Canadian students and permanent residents or $7,490.88 for international students.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> International students without any external funding that meet the general eligibility criteria will be supported with guaranteed funding of up to $3,200 per year.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Tuition for professional Master's programs varies.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_representation">Student representation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Student representation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UBC undergraduate students within the Vancouver campus are represented by the <a href="/wiki/Alma_Mater_Society_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia" title="Alma Mater Society of the University of British Columbia" class="mw-redirect">Alma Mater Society of the University of British Columbia</a>, or AMS. The society's mandate is to improve the quality of educational, social, and personal lives of UBC students. The executive ? composed of the President; Vice President, External Affairs; Vice President, Administration; Vice President, Finance; and Vice President, Academic and University Affairs ? are responsible for lobbying the UBC administration on behalf of the student body, providing services, such as the AMS/GSS Health and Dental Plan, supporting and administering student clubs, and maintaining the Student Union Building (aka SUB) and the services it houses. Recently, the AMS has undertaken an initiative to construct a new Student Union Building (SUB) with a cost of $103 million, of which $80 million is paid by student fees, with 50% more space compared to the current SUB.</p> 
     <p>Graduate Students are represented by the Graduate Student Society (GSS) which operates as an independent entity. The GSS is governed by a council representing each graduate program and an executive elected by graduate students as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_facilities">Student facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Student facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UBC_SUB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/UBC_SUB.jpg/300px-UBC_SUB.jpg" width="300" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/UBC_SUB.jpg/450px-UBC_SUB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/UBC_SUB.jpg/600px-UBC_SUB.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UBC_SUB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Student Union Building on the left, and the War Memorial Gym on the right
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The heart of student activity at UBC Vancouver is the centrally located Student Union Building, which houses offices of many clubs, half a dozen restaurants and caf&eacute;s, a pub (&quot;The Pit&quot;), a nightclub (&quot;The Gallery&quot;), the inexpensive 425-seat Norman Bouchard Memorial Theatre (&quot;The Norm Theatre&quot;), several shops and a post office. The majority of the outlets and shops in the SUB are run by the AMS, however the addition of major corporate outlets in recent years by UBC Food Services has generated some controversy. The SUB Art Gallery contains mostly students' work. An underground bus loop slated to replace the &quot;Grassy Knoll&quot; beside the SUB, did not receive funding by <a href="/wiki/TransLink_(British_Columbia)" title="TransLink (British Columbia)">Translink</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bus_Loop_Letter_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bus_Loop_Letter-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result, the bus loop project has been cancelled by the administration, although the rest of the renovations of the University Boulevard Neighbourhood are still under consideration.</p> 
     <p>Other student facilities on campus include the Ladha Science Student Centre, which was funded through a donation from Abdul Ladha, a levy from all Science undergraduate students, the VP Students, and the Dean of Science, and the Meekison Arts Student Space, which is located in the Faculty of Art's Buchanan D building. The UBC Bookstore has two locations on the Vancouver campus, the main store at 6200 University Boulevard, and one at the <a href="/wiki/Sauder_School_of_Business" title="Sauder School of Business">Sauder School of Business</a>. There are also stores at the Okanagan and Robson Square Campuses. The Bookstore provides a range of products and services. It returns a large dividend back to UBC each year which is re-invested in the campus or in student and community organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_organizations">Greek organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Greek organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>While UBC's Greek system is somewhat smaller than its counterparts in the United States, it does offer the largest and most active Greek system in Canada. There is a total of 18 Greek organizations. An InterFraternal Council (IFC) is recognized as a club by the Alma Mater Society and meetings of the fraternities under IFC occur at their respective fraternity houses each week. Greek life has its own division within UBC REC]<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> and intense competition between the 9 Fraternities for the title of top Athletic Fraternity occur.</p> 
     <p>There are nine international fraternities on campus, the first of which, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Delta Phi">Alpha Delta Phi</a>, was established in 1926. However Alpha Delta Phi was preceded by several local fraternities on campus. Other fraternities include <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Kappa_Epsilon" title="Delta Kappa Epsilon">Delta Kappa Epsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psi_Upsilon" title="Psi Upsilon">Psi Upsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beta_Theta_Pi" title="Beta Theta Pi">Beta Theta Pi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Phi_Delta_Theta" title="Phi Delta Theta">Phi Delta Theta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Gamma_Delta" title="Phi Gamma Delta">Phi Gamma Delta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Sigma" title="Kappa Sigma">Kappa Sigma</a>.</p> 
     <p>The National Panhellenic Conference (NPC) member organizations (sororities) on campus are overseen by the Panhellenic Council.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> All sororities have a chapter room in the Panhellenic House on Wesbrook Mall; the building also offers housing for 72 college women, with preference given to sorority members.</p> 
     <p>The eight sororities on the Vancouver campus include <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Pi" title="Alpha Delta Pi">Alpha Delta Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Delta" title="Alpha Gamma Delta">Alpha Gamma Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Omicron_Pi" title="Alpha Omicron Pi">Alpha Omicron Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi" title="Alpha Phi">Alpha Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Gamma" title="Delta Gamma">Delta Gamma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamma_Phi_Beta" title="Gamma Phi Beta">Gamma Phi Beta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Theta" title="Kappa Alpha Theta">Kappa Alpha Theta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Gamma" title="Kappa Kappa Gamma">Kappa Kappa Gamma</a>. The current Panhellenic total is 81. Chapter meetings are held in the chapter's respective rooms each week or in classrooms and Greek-wide or campus-wide events are attended by members of all the sororities and fraternities. Formal recruitment for the sororities begin during the second week of September and is a 4-day process consisting of: Tours (first 2 days), Invitationals and Preference.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Phrateres" title="Phrateres">Phrateres</a> has traditionally been affiliated with the Greek system since its installation at UBC in 1935. Historical records indicate that for many years, members identified themselves, and were recognized as Greek. Members interacted with fraternities on a similar basis as the sororities, and participated in many Greek events, such as Songfest and exchanges. However, they presently operate as a self-governing organization under the Alma Mater Society with the closure of their international headquarters in 2001.</p> 
     <p>Moreover, UBC was ranked among Canada's top <a href="/wiki/Party_schools" title="Party schools" class="mw-redirect">party schools</a> by the website <i>Ask Men</i>. In the latest ranking, UBC was ranked 7th, ahead of <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University" title="Queen's University">Queen's University</a> and below <a href="/wiki/Concordia_University" title="Concordia University">Concordia University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residences">Residences</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Residences">edit</a>]</span></h3>

       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Dene_Totem_Park.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Dene House at Totem Park
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG/220px-Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG/330px-Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG/440px-Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Marine_Drive_Residence.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Marine Drive
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>According to a 2009 UBC Student Housing Study, UBC currently provides approximately 8680 beds on the Point Grey campus for an on-campus student population of about 11,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-housing-study_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-housing-study-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> The UBC administration has recognized the need for more student housing on campus, forecasting the need for 6400 new beds on campus within the next 20 years, and has expanded housing with the opening of the Marine Drive towers and the MBA house residence on South Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-housing-study_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-housing-study-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of the 2012?2013 school year, there are two <a href="/wiki/Dormitory" title="Dormitory">dormitory</a> style residences on campus, primarily for first and second-year students: Totem Park and Place Vanier.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Totem Park, housing about 1757 students, consists of eight dormitory buildings (Nootka, Dene, Haida, Salish, Kwakiutl, Shuswap, H?m'l?s?m' and Q'?l???n Houses), and a Commons Block (Coquihalla). All houses, except Shuswap, are co-ed, with alternating men's and women's floors; Shuswap house has co-ed floors. Both H?m'l?s?m' and Q'?l???n houses were opened to residents of Totem Park in September 2011 and consist of single rooms with semi-private or private washrooms in contrast to the other house's communal floor washrooms.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Place Vanier, housing 1370 people, consists of 12 blocks constructed in 1959 (Robson House), 1960 (Okanagan, Sherwood Lett, Mackenzie, Ross, Hamber and Mawdsley Houses), 1961 (Kootenay House), 1968 (Cariboo and Tweedsmuir Houses), 2002 (Korea-UBC House) and 2003 (Tec de Monterrey-UBC House). The buildings vary from Male and Female only, to alternating gender floors, as well as fully mixed floors. The residences have both single and double rooms, with each floor having a lounge and communal bathrooms.</p> 
     <p>Students nineteen and above have suite-style residence options on the Point Grey campus. The <a href="/wiki/Walter_Gage" title="Walter Gage">Gage</a> Towers consist of three 17-floor towers (North, South and East) primarily for second, third, and fourth-year undergraduate students. It consists of three interconnected towers (North, South, and East) as well as single student housing (both studio, and apartment) in a building. The towers are composed of &quot;quads&quot;: four separate pods, each consisting of six individual bedrooms, a bathroom and a kitchen-dining area.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Adjacent to the Acadia Park residence area on the east part of campus is Fairview Crescent, a residence primarily for second- and third-year undergraduate students, and many graduate students as well. The residence consists of an L-shaped pedestrian-only street lined with 4, 5 and six-student (a mix of single-sex and co-ed) townhouses. The Beanery coffee shop is in the middle of the residence.</p> 
     <p>The Thunderbird residences are primarily for graduate students and fourth-year undergraduate students; they are located at the southern edge of the academic core campus. The Ritsumeikan-UBC House is a residence with a Japanese cultural setting, named for <a href="/wiki/Ritsumeikan_University" title="Ritsumeikan University">Ritsumeikan University</a>. It houses Japanese exchange students and Canadian students, who participate in unique inter-cultural programmes. The residence's <a href="/wiki/Tatami" title="Tatami">tatami</a> room is used for practice sessions by the UBC <a href="/wiki/Urasenke" title="Urasenke">Urasenke</a> <a href="/wiki/Japanese_tea_ceremony" title="Japanese tea ceremony">Japanese tea ceremony</a> club. Two Canadian students are typically paired with two Japanese exchange students.</p> 
     <p>The newest addition to UBC Vancouver's student housing is the Marine Drive Residence, situated on the west side of campus slightly south of Place Vanier. The first phase, consisting of Building 1 (an 18-floor tower) and Building 2 (a five-floor building commonly called the &quot;Podium&quot;) opened fall 2005, and is the most expensive residence on campus. In February 2006, the Board of Governors approved plans for the second phase of Marine Drive, finally putting an end to the debacle caused by concerns over the view of Wreck beach (Phase I's Building 1 was reduced from 20 floors to 18 because of this). Phase II consists of Buildings 4 through 6 (two towers and another &quot;Podium&quot;, respectively), and also the Commonsblock. Buildings 4 through 6 were all open to students as of September 2008. A separate Commonsblock (the current Front Desk being located in building 1) was completed in summer 2009, and contains similar services to the Commonsblocks of other residences, such as exercise, game, and study rooms. Construction at Marine Drive was completed in February 2010, with the opening of a restaurant in building 4.</p> 
     <p>The university has two colleges dedicated to accommodation for graduate students, postdoctoral fellows and visiting scholars: St. John's College<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Green_College,_University_of_British_Columbia" title="Green College, University of British Columbia">Green College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg/220px-Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg/330px-Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg/440px-Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Olympic_Hockey_at_UBC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> UBC's Doug Mitchell Thunderbird Sports Centre during the 
        <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of British Columbia's sports teams are called the <a href="/wiki/UBC_Thunderbirds" title="UBC Thunderbirds">Thunderbirds</a>. The Thunderbirds participate in the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sports" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sports" class="mw-redirect">CIS's</a> <a href="/wiki/Canada_West_Universities_Athletic_Association" title="Canada West Universities Athletic Association">Canada West Universities Athletic Association</a> for most varsity sports. However, several varsity teams at UBC compete in the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Intercollegiate_Athletics" title="National Association of Intercollegiate Athletics">National Association of Intercollegiate Athletics</a>. UBC is considering joining the <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_II_(NCAA)" title="Division II (NCAA)">Division II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> With a long history of competing in sports, the Thunderbirds have garnered a number of championships. In particular, the women swimmers who had represented UBC had brought back 22 conference championships and 16 national championships.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of British Columbia has a number of athletic facilities open to both their varsity teams as well as to their students. The stadium with the largest seating capacity at UBC is the Doug Mitchell Thunderbird Sports Centre. The Doug Mitchell Thunderbird Sports Centre is home to the varsity ice hockey teams and was also used as a venue for the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Other facilities at UBC includes <a href="/wiki/Thunderbird_Stadium" title="Thunderbird Stadium">Thunderbird Stadium</a>, home to the university's football and soccer varsity teams, UBC Aquatic Centre, home to the university's swimming teams, the War Memorial Gymnasium, home to the university's basketball and volleyball varsity teams and Thunderbird Park, home to the university's many other outdoor varsity teams.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has also had a long history of sending a number of students to represent their countries at the Olympics. Since having its first athlete sent to the Olympics in 1928, a total of 231 individuals from UBC have represented their respective countries at the Olympics. The total number of individual medals athletes from UBC had won was 61, with 19 gold, 21 silver and 24 bronze. The majority of these medals won had come from the sport of rowing.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fight_song">Fight song</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Fight song">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Notable among a number of songs commonly played and sung at various events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>, and athletic games are: &quot;Hail, U.B.C&quot; with words and music by Harold King and &quot;High on Olympus&quot; with words by D.C. Morton and music by J.C.F. Haeffner.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_events">Campus events</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Campus events">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Rosegarden_ubc.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Rosegarden_ubc.jpg/320px-Rosegarden_ubc.jpg" width="320" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Rosegarden_ubc.jpg/480px-Rosegarden_ubc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Rosegarden_ubc.jpg/640px-Rosegarden_ubc.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Rosegarden_ubc.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> UBC Rose Garden.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>A small number of large-scale, campus-wide events occur annually at UBC which are organized by university institutions, the AMS, and student constituencies of various faculties and departments. UBC Orientations organizes several events for first-year students, such as Imagine UBC, GALA, and UBC Jump Start. Imagine UBC is an orientation day and <a href="/wiki/Pep_rally" title="Pep rally">pep rally</a> for first-year undergraduate students that replaces the first day of September classes at UBC Vancouver.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Several group athletic events take place at UBC every year. Storm the Wall is an <a href="/wiki/Intramural" title="Intramural" class="mw-redirect">intramural</a> relay race put on by UBC REC in April, culminating in the climbing of a 12-foot (3.7&nbsp;m) wall. Day of the Longboat is an <a href="/wiki/Intramural" title="Intramural" class="mw-redirect">intramural</a> event put on at the end of September/early October by UBC REC. It is a major voyageur canoe race with teams competing in a 2&nbsp;km paddle around the waters of Jericho Sailing Centre. The program is operated by over 120 volunteer students and staff who are responsible for operating every aspect of this program. UBC REC's student administrators fill various roles including event planning, sport officiating, public relations and building supervision.</p> 
     <p>Faculty constituencies, such as the Arts Undergraduate Society (AUS) and Science Undergraduate Society (SUS), hold events annually. Many of the major constituencies, such as for Arts, Science, and Engineering, hold their own faculty weeks to celebrate their faculties. The events may include keynote speeches, merchandise sales, and dances. Arts County Fair was an annual concert and party on the last day of classes in April, put on by the AUS and occurring at Thunderbird Stadium. Past headliners have included <a href="/wiki/Sam_Roberts" title="Sam Roberts">Sam Roberts</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_New_Pornographers" title="The New Pornographers">The New Pornographers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Metric_(band)" title="Metric (band)">Metric</a>. Due to increasing financial difficulties (mostly resulting from mounting security and related costs) the AUS announced they would not continue the event in 2008. In its place, the Alma Mater Society of UBC hosted the AMS Block Party to celebrate the end of classes.</p> 
     <p>A number of unofficial 'traditions,' exist at UBC: jumping from the UBC Aquatic Centre's outdoor 10-metre diving board late at night; and frequent repainting of the Engineering <a href="/wiki/Cairn" title="Cairn">cairn</a>, refashioning its large red-and-white 'E' into other letters representative of other faculties, clubs, and groups.</p> 
     <p>In March 2012, UBC was the partner Host University of the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_World_Model_United_Nations" title="Harvard World Model United Nations">Harvard World Model United Nations</a> Conference (WorldMUN 2012 Vancouver). As the world's largest student-organized Model UN conference, this was also the largest student conference to have ever been organized by UBC and the largest student conference on Canadian soil.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> There were 2,200 student delegates and nearly 200 faculty advisors from 270 universities from over 60 countries. The organizing committee amassed over 500 student volunteers from across the UBC campus and the local student community to execute the week-long event.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a>]</span></h2>

     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Beverley_McLachlin_(crop).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Beverley_McLachlin_%28crop%29.jpg/200px-Beverley_McLachlin_%28crop%29.jpg" width="200" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Beverley_McLachlin_%28crop%29.jpg/300px-Beverley_McLachlin_%28crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Beverley_McLachlin_%28crop%29.jpg/400px-Beverley_McLachlin_%28crop%29.jpg 2x" /></a>

     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_British_Columbia_people" title="List of University of British Columbia people">List of University of British Columbia people</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chancellors_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia" title="List of Chancellors of the University of British Columbia">List of Chancellors of the University of British Columbia</a>&nbsp;and 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_University_of_British_Columbia" title="List of Presidents of the University of British Columbia">List of Presidents of the University of British Columbia</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Throughout UBC's history, faculty, alumni, and former students have played prominent roles in many different fields. Many UBC alumni and faculty have gone on to win awards including seven <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prizes" title="Nobel Prizes" class="mw-redirect">Nobel Prizes</a> and 67 <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarships" title="Rhodes Scholarships" class="mw-redirect">Rhodes Scholarships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-facts1_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts1-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Former alumni have won Nobel Prizes: <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mundell" title="Robert Mundell">Robert Mundell</a> (Economic Sciences) who graduated from the <a href="/wiki/UBC_Department_of_Economics" title="UBC Department of Economics">UBC Department of Economics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bertram_Brockhouse" title="Bertram Brockhouse">Bertram Brockhouse</a> (Physics).<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> Five former faculty members of the UBC have also received a Nobel Prize: <a href="/wiki/Michael_Smith_(chemist)" title="Michael Smith (chemist)">Michael Smith</a> (Chemistry), <a href="/wiki/Har_Gobind_Khorana" title="Har Gobind Khorana">Har Gobind Khorana</a> (Physiology or Medicine), <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Kahneman" title="Daniel Kahneman">Daniel Kahneman</a> (Economics), <a href="/wiki/Hans_G._Dehmelt" title="Hans G. Dehmelt" class="mw-redirect">Hans G. Dehmelt</a> (Physics), and <a href="/wiki/Carl_Wieman" title="Carl Wieman">Carl Wieman</a> (Physics.)<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Many former students have gained local and national prominence in government. The university had produced two Canadian Prime Ministers, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Campbell" title="Kim Campbell">Kim Campbell</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Turner" title="John Turner">John Turner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> Canadian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Joe_Clark" title="Joe Clark">Joe Clark</a> briefly attended UBC law.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_Stanley" title="George Stanley">George Stanley</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_New_Brunswick" title="Lieutenant Governor of New Brunswick">Lieutenant Governor of New Brunswick</a> and creator of the current <a href="/wiki/Canadian_flag" title="Canadian flag" class="mw-redirect">Canadian flag</a> had also served as faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Alumni <a href="/wiki/Mike_Harcourt" title="Mike Harcourt">Mike Harcourt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glen_Clark" title="Glen Clark">Glen Clark</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ujjal_Dosanjh" title="Ujjal Dosanjh">Ujjal Dosanjh</a> have been Premiers of British Columbia:,<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> People of <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia_Faculty_of_Law" title="University of British Columbia Faculty of Law">UBC Law</a> have also served on the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Supreme Court of Canada</a>: former faculty member <a href="/wiki/Beverley_McLachlin" title="Beverley McLachlin">Beverley McLachlin</a> and alumnus <a href="/wiki/Frank_Iacobucci" title="Frank Iacobucci">Frank Iacobucci</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Canadian academic, science broadcaster and environmental activist <a href="/wiki/David_Suzuki" title="David Suzuki">David Suzuki</a> was a professor in the genetics department at UBC from 1963 until his retirement in 2001. <a href="/wiki/Joel_Bakan" title="Joel Bakan">Joel Bakan</a>, author of <a href="/wiki/The_Corporation_(film)" title="The Corporation (film)">The Corporation: The Pathological Pursuit of Profit and Power</a> is a professor at the faculty of law. Psychologist <a href="/wiki/Albert_Bandura" title="Albert Bandura">Albert Bandura</a> is an alumnus of UBC. Actress <a href="/wiki/Evangeline_Lilly" title="Evangeline Lilly">Evangeline Lilly</a> attended UBC, earning her degree in International Relations. Author and historian <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Berton" title="Pierre Berton">Pierre Berton</a> majored in history at UBC. Man-in-Motion <a href="/wiki/Rick_Hansen" title="Rick Hansen">Rick Hansen</a> was the first student with a physical disability to graduate in <a href="/wiki/Physical_education" title="Physical education">physical education</a> from UBC. Opera singers <a href="/wiki/Ben_Heppner" title="Ben Heppner">Ben Heppner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Judith_Forst" title="Judith Forst">Judith Forst</a> studied music at UBC.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_British_Columbia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <ul> 
      <li>William A. Bruneau, <i>A Matter of Identities: A History of the UBC Faculty Association, 1920?1990</i>. Vancouver: University of British Columbia Faculty Association, 1990.</li> 
      <li>William A. Bruneau &quot;Toward a New Collective Biography: The University of British Columbia Professoriate, 1915?1945.&quot; Canadian Journal of Education 19, no. 1 (Winter 1994).</li> 
      <li>Eric Damer and Herbert Rosengarten. &quot;UBC: The First 100 Years.&quot; Vancouver: Friesens, 2009.</li> 
      <li>Michiel Horn.&quot;Under the Gaze of George Vancouver: The University of British Columbia and the Provincial Government, 1913?1939.&quot; BC Studies 83 (Autumn 1989).</li> 
      <li>William C. Gibson <i>Wesbrook &amp; His University</i> (Vancouver: University of British Columbia Press)</li> 
      <li>H.T. Logan, <i>Tuum Est: A History of the University of British Columbia.</i> Vancouver: University of British Columbia, 1958.</li> 
      <li>Wayne Skene. &quot;UBC: a Portrait.&quot; Vancouver: Tribute Books, 2003.</li> 
      <li>Lee Stewart. <i>&quot;It's Up to You&quot;: Women at UBC in the Early Years.</i> Vancouver: University of British Columbia Press, 1990.</li> 
      <li>George Woodcock &amp; Tim Fitzharris. <i>The University of British Columbia ? A Souvenir</i>. (Toronto: Oxford University Press, 1986).</li> 
     </ul>
